### Question 47: I have 112 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from EL. Can I graduate?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright, a student must earn a minimum of 128 credit hours. You have 112 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from Experiential Learning (EL), which totals 128 credit hours. Therefore, you have met the minimum requirement to graduate. The 16 credits from EL count towards your graduation requirement, as per the Experiential Learning Program (ELP) requirement that all full-time, undergraduate, degree-seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. So, based on the information provided, you are eligible to graduate.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
of credit hours a student successfully completes with a grade of D or higher for letter grade options and a Pass for Pass/No Pass options. Attempted credits are the credit hours students enroll in and are recorded in the transcript, regardless of whether they complete the courses or pass them. This includes all courses for which a student receives a grade, including withdrawals (W), incompletes (I), repeats (RP), and failures (F). See section 4 for more details on different types of grades. To graduate with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright, a student must earn a minimum of 128 credit hours.  The typical full-time course load is 16 credit hours per term or 4 courses of 4 credit hours each. In order to make standard progress toward completing the degree, students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. Students who wish to take fewer than 12 or more than 16 credit hours in one term must submit the Petition for Alternative Course Load or

### Question 48: I have received an offer to attend an international conference but lack funding. What school funds can I apply for?  
### Answer: 

The University acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Circumstances that may fall into this category are: • Exceptional medical circumstances, e.g., hospitalization or incapacitation through injury, illness, or mental health crisis. • Close bereavement, e.g., partner, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, and grandchild. Housemates or very close friends may also be considered as ‘close’, though evidence of the relationship may be required. • Victim of a serious crime • Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student • Exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties e.g., major transport incidents, cancelled flights. This does not include everyday issues, e.g., traffic congestion, missed buses or trains. • Legal proceedings requiring attendance.

The University may provide financial assistance or support in exceptional circumstances. Students facing financial difficulties due to unforeseen events such as those listed above may be eligible for support. This could include funding for travel, accommodation, or other related expenses associated with attending an international conference.

To apply for school funds, students should follow the University's established procedures for requesting financial assistance. This typically involves:

1. **Submitting a Request:** Students should complete the appropriate form for requesting financial assistance, which is usually available on the University's website or through the relevant department (e.g., Student Financial Services, Academic Affairs).

2. **Providing Documentation:** As part of the application, students will need to provide documentation to support their request. This might include:

   - A letter explaining the circumstances and the relevance of attending the conference.
   - Proof of the conference offer, such as an acceptance letter or invitation.
   - Evidence of the financial hardship, such as a current bank statement or a letter from a financial advisor.
   - Any other relevant documentation, such as medical certificates or police reports if applicable.

3. **Meeting Deadlines:** There may be specific deadlines for applying for financial assistance, so it is important to submit the request well in advance of the conference date.

4. **Review and Approval:** The University will review the application and supporting documents. Approval is not guaranteed and is based on the merits of the case and the availability of funds.

5. **Communication:** Students should keep in touch with the financial aid office to follow up on the status of their application and to understand any conditions attached to the award, such as reporting requirements after the conference.

It is important to note that while the University may offer support in exceptional circumstances, it is also important to explore other sources of funding, such as external scholarships, grants, or crowdfunding platforms.

In summary, students facing financial barriers to attending an international conference should first review the University's policies on financial assistance and then submit a detailed and well-documented request for support. They should also consider other funding opportunities to maximize their chances of attending the conference.

### Question 50: In a regular semester, can I take only 2 courses? If so, how will my tuition fees be affected?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you can take only 2 courses in a regular semester. However, it's important to note that maintaining full-time enrollment status typically requires registering for a minimum of 12 credits per term. Taking only 2 courses usually means you will be considered part-time, which may affect your tuition fees and financial aid eligibility. According to the provided context, no reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits. Therefore, if you are authorized to take only 2 courses due to exceptional circumstances, your tuition fees will likely remain unchanged, but you should check the "Fees & Charges Guide" for undergraduate students to confirm any specific policies regarding part-time enrollment. Additionally, you should be aware that course withdrawals may affect your financial aid eligibility if they result in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment. Always consult with the Registrar's Office and the Financial Aid Office to understand the full implications of taking fewer than the standard course load.

### Question 51: Can I pursue 3 majors?  
### Answer: 

Fulbright's academic structure does not explicitly state a limit on the number of majors a student can pursue. However, it does outline the requirements and rules for managing multiple majors, minors, and Exploratory requirements. According to the provided information:

- Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major.
- If two majors share cross-listed or tagged courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim.
- For instance, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C.

This implies that while there is no explicit limit on the number of majors a student can pursue, the university does provide mechanisms to manage the overlap and requirements between multiple majors. However, the practicality and feasibility of pursuing three majors would depend on the specific course offerings, the student's schedule, and the ability to meet all the requirements without exceeding the maximum length of study (8 years).

Given the structure and flexibility provided, it is theoretically possible to pursue three majors, but students should carefully plan their course selections to ensure they meet all requirements without overloading their academic schedule or exceeding the maximum time to complete their studies. It is also important to consider the potential for a heavy course load and the potential impact on the quality of education and overall student experience.

In summary, while there is no explicit prohibition against pursuing three majors, students should carefully plan their academic path and stay within the guidelines provided to ensure a successful and manageable academic journey.

### Question 52: How can I change my major declaration?  
### Answer: 

To change your major declaration, you should follow these steps:

1. **Understand the University Policy**: The university-wide policy states that majors and minors may have additional policies and requirements. These are typically outlined in the major’s description and flowchart or handbook.

2. **Consult the Major’s Description**: Review the major’s description and flowchart or handbook to understand any additional policies and requirements specific to the major you wish to change into.

3. **Contact the Major Coordinator**: Reach out to the major coordinator for the new major. They can provide you with detailed information about the process, prerequisites, and any necessary steps to change your major.

4. **Approval Process**: Any exception to the university policy must be approved by the major coordinator and the Dean’s Office. This may involve submitting a formal request, which could include a letter explaining your reasons for wanting to change your major.

5. **Academic Advisor or Dean’s Office**: Your academic advisor or the Dean’s Office can assist you in navigating the process. They may also help you with the paperwork and ensure that all necessary approvals are obtained.

6. **Follow the Approval Process**: Complete any required forms and gather any necessary documentation, such as a letter from your academic advisor or a letter explaining your reasons for the change.

7. **Submit the Request**: Submit your request to change your major to the appropriate office, typically the Registrar’s Office, along with any supporting documentation.

8. **Wait for Approval**: After submission, wait for the approval process to be completed. The Registrar's Office will inform you of the decision.

9. **Adhere to the Decision**: If your request is approved, make sure to adhere to any conditions set forth by the major coordinator or the Dean’s Office, such as completing any additional prerequisites.

Remember, the process may vary slightly depending on the specific requirements of your current major and the major you wish to switch to, so it’s important to stay in close communication with your academic advisor and the major coordinator throughout the process.

The references provided do not specifically address the process of changing a major but rather outline the general policy regarding course load adjustments, grade appeals, and exceptions to university policies. Therefore, these references are irrelevant to the question of changing a major declaration.

### Question 53: What is the process of delaying my payment?  
### Answer: 

If a student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, they should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. The student should discuss their situation and explore options such as a late payment arrangement or an extension of the tuition fee payment deadline. The Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from the student before placing them in an absence status. It is important for the student to communicate their situation proactively to avoid being placed on an Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) which could result in being unable to register for new courses or participate in classes or a Work-Study Program during the current term. The student should also be aware that a leave does not clear their bill, and they may lose eligibility for scholarships. After the approved period of absence, the student must contact the Registrar’s Office to confirm their plan to return by registering for course(s) or have their leave extended, if applicable. The extension must be endorsed by the Registrar’s Office and approved by the Dean’s Office.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 15]
balance is clear. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, the student should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. After the approved period of absence, a student is put on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term if the Registrar’s Office receives no response of return confirmation or no registration in the returning term. After one term of Admin LOA, a student is officially withdrawn from Fulbright unless they have contacted the Registrar’s Office and confirmed the plan to return by registering for course(s) or have been granted a leave extension, a maximum of another term. The extension must be endorsed by the Registrar’s Office and approved by the Dean’s Office.

### Question 54: Which major has the fewest requirements?  
### Answer: 

The major with the fewest requirements is the minor. The minor requires students to take a total of six courses (24 credits), whereas the major requires students to take a total of ten courses (56 credits). The minor courses include: one programming course (4 credits), one 100-level or 200-level CS course (4 credits), CS 201 – Data Structures & Algorithms (4 credits), one intermediate course (4 credits), one 200-level or 300-level CS course (4 credits), and one advanced course (4 credits). The major courses include: CS 101: Introduction to Programming (4 credits), CS 201: Data Structures & Algorithms (4 credits), CS 203: Computer Organization (4 credits), MATH 202: Discrete Math (4 credits), three intermediate courses (12 credits), CS 302: Algorithms & Theory of Computing (4 credits), four advanced courses (16 credits), and two capstone courses (8 credits).

### Question 55: How many courses can I take in total?  
### Answer: 

The total number of courses required to graduate is 128 credits. However, courses in Physical Education and Political courses do not count toward this requirement. Additionally, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be double-counted if a student has multiple majors (or a major and a minor) that share cross-listed or tagged courses. This 8-credit limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor), and it does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim overall. For example, a student could major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. Therefore, the total number of courses a student can take, considering double-counting, is 128 credits minus the credits from Physical Education and Political courses, plus any double-counted credits up to the 8-credit limit per each pair of majors or major/minor. The maximum time to complete the program is 8 years, given the maximum length of study is double the standard duration.

### Question 56: How many courses in a semester can I take in total?  
### Answer: 

The question asks about the total number of courses a student can take in a semester. According to the provided context, there is no specific mention of a maximum number of courses a student can take in a semester. The context discusses course loads and credit hours, but it does not provide a direct answer to the question of how many courses a student can take in total.

The context does mention that "up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements" when discussing double-counting for majors and minors (13.3). However, this information pertains to the number of courses that can be double-counted, not the total number of courses a student can take.

The context also mentions course load and credit hours (3.1), but it does not specify a maximum number of courses. Typically, a full-time student load is considered to be 12-18 credits per semester, which generally equates to 4-6 courses, but this can vary depending on the institution and the specific program requirements.

Therefore, based on the provided information, the answer to the question "How many courses in a semester can I take in total?" is not directly answered in the given context. The standard practice is that a full-time student might take 4-6 courses per semester, but this is not explicitly stated in the provided text. The answer is: The context does not provide a specific number of courses a student can take in a semester. Typically, a full-time student might take 4-6 courses per semester, but this is not explicitly stated in the provided text.

### Question 58: How can I audit a course?  
### Answer: 

You cannot audit a course. Auditing a course is not an option provided by most colleges and universities. Instead, you must register for the course as a pass/no pass (P/NP) or for a letter grade. If you want to take a course without the pressure of getting a grade, you might consider registering for it as pass/no pass. However, this option varies by institution, and some schools do not offer it for all courses. To find out if you can register for a course as pass/no pass, check your school's academic policies or consult with your academic advisor. If you're interested in attending the lectures and participating in the course without the commitment of completing assignments or taking exams, you might consider simply attending the class without registering. However, this is usually not officially recognized by the institution and may not provide any academic credit or proof of attendance. Always check with your institution's policies regarding auditing courses and registering for pass/no pass options.

### Question 59: If I'm going for a double major then how many courses can be double count maximum?  
### Answer: 

If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross-listed or tagged courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged.

### Question 60: Can you give me the grade translation from alphabetic to numerical?  
### Answer: 

The grade translation from alphabetic to numerical is as follows: Letter Grade Grade Point Grade Category Percentage A 4.0 Outstanding 94-100% A- 3.7 Excellent 90-93.9% B+ 3.3 Good 87-89.9% B 3.0 Good 83-86.9% B- 2.7 Good 80-83.9% C+ 2.3 Satisfactory 77-79.9% C 2.0 Satisfactory 73-76.9% C- 1.7 Satisfactory 70-72.9% D+ 1.3 Poor 67-69.9% D 1.0 Poor 63-66.9% D- 0.7 Poor 60-62.9% F 0.0 Failure Below 60%

GRADING: At Fulbright, the majority of courses apply a standard letter grade ranging from ‘A’ to ‘F.’ Grade points are assigned to letter grades according to the following scale (unless otherwise decided by faculty in individual courses): Letter Grade Grade Point Grade Category Percentage

o The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting to the P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term. o A grade of ‘C-’ or higher will be counted as a Pass. Courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. o Any grade below a ‘C-’ will be counted as a No Pass. No credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. • I = Incomplete: If a student is unable to complete the work in a course because of illness, family emergency, or other exceptional circumstances (see Section 12), a temporary grade of ‘I’ (Incomplete) may be awarded by the faculty until unfinished course requirements are completed. ### Question 62: Why and how am I getting academic suspension?  
### Answer: 

You are getting academic suspension because you failed to fulfill all the requirements of your Learning Contract while on Academic Probation. The process involves the Dean’s Office establishing conditions that you must meet prior to returning to Fulbright. Academic Suspension typically lasts for one term or one academic year, and you may be suspended a maximum of two times. If you are suspended a third time, your enrollment in the program will be canceled, and you will need to apply for re-admission. The re-admission decision is made by the Dean’s Office in consultation with appropriate faculty and staff members. To return, you must submit a letter with your application for re-admission that addresses the reasons for your suspensions and the measures you have taken to address those reasons.

### Question 63: How does the P/NP grade work?  
### Answer: 

The P/NP grade option allows students to take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis. To elect this option, students must complete a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form and submit it to the Registrar’s Office before a specific deadline. Once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back. Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements.

A grade of 'C-' or higher will be counted as a Pass, and courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Any grade below a 'C-' will be counted as a No Pass, and no credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript, and courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.

The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting the final grade to P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term. All courses for which a P/NP, I, W, or RP grade is awarded are excluded from the GPA calculation.

### Question 64: How many courses can I take as P/NP at maximum and how will it contribute to the official transcript GPA?  
### Answer: 

Students can take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) on a Pass/No Pass basis in one academic year. These courses do not contribute to the official transcript GPA because all courses for which a P/NP, I, W, or RP grade is awarded are excluded from the GPA calculation. The P/NP grades do not apply to core courses and cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements. Once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back. The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting the grades to P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term. A grade of ‘C-’ or higher will be counted as a Pass, while any grade below a ‘C-’ will be counted as a No Pass. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript, and courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.

For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 65: I've failed the GWP due to personal reasons so will it count toward the 144 maximum credits I can have?  
### Answer: 

No, a failing grade (F) will count toward the 144 maximum credits you can have. According to the provided context, a failing grade (F) is awarded if a student does not complete the remaining course work by the agreed-upon deadline after receiving an Incomplete grade (I). The context states that "otherwise, the student will be awarded a letter grade, which may be an ‘F’, based upon the work completed by the deadline." This means that if you fail to complete the course requirements within the given timeframe, an 'F' will be recorded on your transcript, which will count toward your total attempted credits for GPA calculation and also toward the 144 maximum credits you can have. The context does not specify any exceptions for personal reasons in this regard. Therefore, the 'F' grade will indeed count toward your total credits, impacting both your GPA and your overall credit limit.

### Question 66: What and how do I get an Academic Warning?  
### Answer: 

An Academic Warning is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. To receive an Academic Warning, the Registrar’s Office sends out an official notification. The student is then required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting where a Learning Contract is created with specific conditions tailored to their individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. It is important to note that three official warnings may result in Disciplinary Action, constituting Academic Probation or Academic Suspension.

The student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. ### Question 67: How can I make reservations of rooms for personal usage?  
### Answer: 

To make reservations of rooms for personal usage, you typically need to follow these steps:

1. Contact the Residential Life Office: Reach out to the Residential Life staff at your institution. They can provide you with information on the reservation process, availability, and any associated fees.

2. Complete the Reservation Form: Fill out any necessary reservation forms provided by the Residential Life Office. This form usually includes details about the dates you wish to reserve the room, your name, and any other relevant information.

3. Submit the Reservation Form: Submit the completed reservation form to the Residential Life Office. You may need to do this in person, by mail, or through an online portal.

4. Pay Any Required Fees: Check if there are any fees associated with reserving the room and make the necessary payment. This could be a one-time fee or a daily rate depending on the policy of your institution.

5. Confirm Your Reservation: After submitting your reservation form and payment, follow up with the Residential Life Office to confirm that your reservation has been processed and is confirmed.

6. Understand the Cancellation Policy: Be aware of the cancellation policy in case you need to change your plans. Some institutions may have specific rules regarding cancellations and refunds.

7. Check-In and Check-Out Procedures: Familiarize yourself with the check-in and check-out procedures provided by the Residential Life Office. This will ensure a smooth experience during your stay.

Remember, the exact process may vary depending on the specific policies and procedures of your institution, so it's important to consult directly with the Residential Life Office for the most accurate information.

### Question 68: Can you provide me with some courses suggestion to take to major in Math?  
### Answer: 

To major in Applied Mathematics, you should start with the foundation courses such as Linear Algebra, Single Variable Calculus, Introduction to Statistics, and Multivariable Calculus. After completing these foundation courses, you should move on to intermediate courses like Probability, Differential Equations, Discrete Mathematics, and Numerical Analysis. For advanced study, consider courses such as Advanced Statistics, Statistical Learning, Stochastic Calculus, Numerical Analysis, Optimization, and Partial Differential Equations. Additionally, you should take at least two applied courses from other majors to broaden your understanding of how mathematics is applied in various fields. These could include courses from Economics, Engineering, or Computer Science such as Game Theory, Signal Systems and Control, Introduction to Machine Learning, and Statistical Learning. Remember to consult with an academic advisor to tailor your course selection to your interests and career goals. Also, consider taking a Pure Mathematics course to deepen your understanding of the abstract concepts that underpin all areas of mathematics. Lastly, participating in research seminars can provide valuable insights into faculty research and opportunities for further study or career paths.

### Question 69: How to declare a major in Computer Science?  
### Answer: 

To formally declare Computer Science as their major, the student must complete at least two Computer Science courses (MATH 202 - Discrete Math is also counted). The major requirements include CS 101: Introduction to Programming (4 credits), CS 201: Data Structures & Algorithms (4 credits), CS 203: Computer Organization (4 credits), MATH 202: Discrete Math (4 credits), three intermediate courses (12 credits), CS 302: Algorithms & Theory of Computing (4 credits), four advanced courses (16 credits), and Capstone I or an additional intermediate or advanced course (4 credits), followed by Capstone II or an additional intermediate or advanced course (4 credits).

### Question 70: I'm currently under a General Work Program for Experiential Learning but the company do not pay me in any form. How can I get the subsidy from Fulbright University?  
### Answer: 

Fulbright University Vietnam's Experiential Learning Program (ELP) offers students the opportunity to earn academic credit for experiential learning experiences. However, the ELP does not appear to provide financial subsidies or payments for students working under the General Work Program for Experiential Learning. The ELP is designed to facilitate academic credit-bearing experiences, not to provide financial compensation for work performed.

The ELP streams are managed by Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and the Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), each responsible for their respective streams. These programs are aimed at enhancing students' learning experiences and may include internships, research projects, community service, and entrepreneurial activities, among others.

To receive academic credit through the ELP, students typically need to:

1. Identify an appropriate experiential learning opportunity that aligns with their academic goals and interests.
2. Work with their academic advisor to ensure the experience meets the criteria for ELP credit.
3. Complete the necessary paperwork and documentation to register for ELP credit.
4. Participate in the experience and fulfill the requirements set by the ELP and their faculty advisor.

Regarding financial compensation, students typically need to secure their own funding or work arrangements. Fulbright University Vietnam does not provide financial subsidies for students working under the ELP. Students may need to explore other sources of financial aid, scholarships, or part-time employment opportunities available to them.

For specific details on the ELP and any potential financial support, students should refer to the official ELP information provided by Fulbright University Vietnam, as mentioned in the context: https://onestop.fulbright.edu.vn/s/article/Experiential-Learning-Program

If a student is facing financial difficulties, they should also consider reaching out to the university's financial aid office to explore available options, such as scholarships, grants, or work-study programs. It's important to note that policies and offerings can change, so it's always best to check the most current information available on the university's website or by contacting the appropriate office directly.

### Question 71: Can you give me the process of making a Capstone for graduation?  
### Answer: 

The process of making a Capstone for graduation involves several key steps, particularly for students pursuing a Capstone by Dissertation or Capstone by Creative Writing. Here's a breakdown based on the provided guidelines:

**Capstone I:**

* **Meet with your advisor:** As early as possible to set a regular meeting schedule and expectations for submissions with a timeline.
* **Active participation in advising processes:** Regularly engage with your advisor to ensure you're on track.
* **End-of-term submission:** This typically includes:
  * **Literature review or annotated bibliography:** A minimum of five pages (2,000 words) summarizing relevant research.
  * **Introduction:** A clear and concise introduction to your project.
  * **Other materials/documents:** These may include questionnaires or other preliminary research materials, decided upon in consultation with your advisors.

**Capstone II:**

* **Focus on production:** This phase involves the actual creation or writing of your project, whether it's a dissertation or a creative work.
* **Documentation of process:** Keep records of your research, development, and production process.
* **Formal presentation requirement:** Prepare a formal presentation of your work, which may be part of the evaluation process.
* **Evaluation criteria:** Your work will be assessed based on the criteria outlined for your specific Capstone track (e.g., dissertation or creative writing).

**General Notes:**

* **Advisors' approval:** Some initial stages of production may begin with advisors' approval.
* **Combination of assessment:** Capstone I is assessed through a combination of your participation in advising processes and an end-of-term submission.
* **Flexibility:** The specific requirements (like the nature of the end-of-term submission) may be decided in consultation with your advisors based on the nature of your project.
* **Timeline:** Adhere to the timeline set with your advisor to ensure timely completion of the Capstone requirements.

The Capstone process is designed to be a culmination of your academic journey, integrating your learning and research into a substantial project. It requires careful planning, active engagement with your advisors, and a commitment to seeing your project through from conception to completion.

### Question 73: How can I graduate with Honor or lie within the top GPA?  
### Answer: 

An honour pass capstone is the key requirement for graduating with Honor. The GPA is calculated by dividing [the sum of (grade points earned * credit hours earned) for each course] by [the total attempted credits for GPA]. All courses for which a P/NP, I, W, or RP grade is awarded are excluded from the GPA calculation. To graduate with Honor, you need to achieve a score of 90 to 100 points in the Capstone course, which includes 85 points for the written thesis and 15 points for the presentation. You should also aim for high grades in all other courses, avoiding grades lower than a 'C-' in core courses and 'D+' or lower in other courses. If you receive a grade lower than 'D+', you may need to repeat the course. Additionally, you should avoid withdrawing from courses (W grade) as it does not affect the GPA. If you receive an 'I' (Incomplete) grade, you must complete the required work to receive a letter grade before the end of the term to avoid it affecting your GPA. Regularly consult with your academic advisor to ensure you are on track to meet the requirements for graduating with Honor.

### Question 74: How many courses can I take with P/NP grade in total?  
### Answer: 

Students can take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
o The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting to the P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term. o A grade of ‘C-’ or higher will be counted as a Pass. Courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. o Any grade below a ‘C-’ will be counted as a No Pass. No credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. • I = Incomplete: If a student is unable to complete the work in a course because of illness, family emergency, or other exceptional circumstances (see Section 12), a temporary grade of ‘I’ (Incomplete) may be awarded by the faculty until unfinished course requirements are completed. The student has until the date agreed upon with the faculty (not to exceed 6 months from the end of the course) to complete all remaining course work; otherwise, the student will be

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis by completing a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form and submitting it to the Registrar’s Office before 4:00 PM on Friday Week 4 of the term (16-week term).  The following conditions apply: o Once a student converts a course grade option to Pass/No Pass, the grade option cannot be changed back. o Pass/No Pass grades do not apply to core courses. They cannot be used to count toward major/minor requirements. o The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting to the P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term. o A grade of ‘C-’ or higher will be counted as a Pass. Courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. o Any grade below a ‘C-’ will be counted as a No Pass. No credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
• Physical Education • Political courses These courses do not count toward the 128-credit requirement. All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 76: How many types of leave of absence are there and how can I have one?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of leave of absence: Personal Leave, Medical Leave, and Administrative Leave of Absence. To have one, you must complete and submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form, along with supporting documents, before the last day of class. Fulbright permits students in Good Academic Standing to apply for a leave of absence for one to two terms. You should also meet with your Academic Advisor to discuss a plan to complete a degree and elaborate on your reasons for taking a Leave of Absence. Normally, a student is not permitted to remain on campus during a period of absence from their studies, but exceptions will be considered on a case-by-case basis.

### Question 77: How can I report violation of Academic environment anonymously?  
### Answer: 

At Fulbright University Vietnam, if you wish to report a violation of the academic environment anonymously, you should follow the outlined procedures in the provided documents. Specifically, if you encounter issues related to academic integrity, academic standing, or any other academic-related concerns, you should:

1. **Document the Incident**: Clearly note down the details of the incident, including dates, times, and any relevant evidence you have.

2. **Use the Academic Standing Form**: If the issue pertains to academic integrity or academic standing (such as academic warning, probation, or suspension), you can use the form provided under section 6 of the Academic Standing document. This form requires you to specify the issue and provides a space for you to explain the situation. Attach any applicable supporting documents to strengthen your report.

3. **Confidentiality Agreement**: Since you wish to remain anonymous, ensure that you adhere to the Confidentiality Agreement mentioned in the context. This agreement ensures that you will not be identified in any proceedings related to your report.

4. **Submit the Report**: Submit the completed form and any supporting documents to the appropriate office (e.g., the Office of Student Affairs or the academic unit involved) for review. Make sure to keep a copy for your records.

5. **Anonymity**: While the context does not explicitly guarantee anonymity, the emphasis on confidentiality in the agreement suggests that your identity will be protected to the best of the university's ability. However, it's important to note that complete anonymity cannot be guaranteed in all circumstances, especially if the reported incident requires investigation and evidence gathering.

6. **Follow-Up**: After submitting your report, you may wish to follow up with the office to ensure they have received it and are taking appropriate action. However, maintain your anonymity by not revealing your identity during this process.

Remember, while the provided documents offer a structured approach to reporting academic violations, the university's commitment to academic integrity and confidentiality should be upheld by all parties involved. If you're unsure about the process, consider reaching out to the Vice President of Student Affairs or another trusted university official for guidance.

### Question 78: Where can I get all forms and pdf related to my academic journey at Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

You can get all forms and PDF related to your academic journey at Fulbright from the Office of the Registrar. The Office of the Registrar typically handles various academic-related processes, including course load requests, course withdrawal requests, incomplete grade requests, credit transfer applications, official activity excused absence requests, undergraduate leave of absence (LOA) applications, and withdrawal from Fulbright forms. Additionally, they manage the exit checklist process which includes forms for academic affairs, residential life, and registrar & billing. For transfer credit applications, you would need to provide detailed information about the courses taken at another institution, including the course curriculum, learning outcomes, and assessments. Always check the official website or contact the Office of the Registrar directly for the most current and comprehensive list of forms and procedures.

### Question 79: What is the school's policy on academic dishonesty, and how are violations handled?  
### Answer: 

The school's policy on academic dishonesty is outlined in the Code of Academic Integrity. Violations are handled by the Registrar's Office informing the Dean’s Office of the case, which then investigates the matter. If the Deans can mediate the issue, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the matter. Dismissal from the school may occur in extraordinary circumstances following multiple written warnings, as determined by the Dean’s Office in consultation with appropriate members of faculty and staff, if a student's academic performance is unsatisfactory or if their behavior represents present harm to others in the Fulbright community.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: CS_Capstone_Guideline_v2_Dec_20_2024.pdf, Page: 2]

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 2]

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 11]
DISMISSAL: In all circumstances, Fulbright’s goal is to support students in the completion of their degree. However, dismissal from Fulbright may occur if a suspended student does not fulfill the conditions of suspension, if a student’s behavior represents present harm to others in the Fulbright community, or if a student’s academic performance is unsatisfactory to the degree that continued enrollment is deemed unsupportable. Such decisions are never taken likely, and dismissal occurs only in extraordinary circumstances following multiple written warnings, as determined by the Dean’s Office in consultation with appropriate members of faculty and staff.

In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the matter.

### Question 80: What are the policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades?  
### Answer: 

Students are required to repeat core courses in the case of receiving the grade F and/or course(s) counted toward major/minor in the case of receiving a grade below ‘C-’. Students may repeat a course if they have received a grade of ‘D+’, ‘D’, ‘F’, or NP for the course or have withdrawn and received a grade of ‘W’. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after having received a grade higher than a ‘D+’ following consultation with the student’s academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar’s Office. Considerations will include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation “RP”, meaning “repeated”, and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless he/she failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. Students shall consult with their Academic/Major Advisor about their program plan if they are considering taking the class for a third time.  

<details>

### Question 81: How does the university accommodate students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance?  
### Answer: 

The university acknowledges that students may experience exceptional circumstances, such as exceptional medical circumstances (including chronic illnesses), close bereavement, being a victim of a serious crime, disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place, and exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties. For medical leave, students must submit the appropriate forms along with medical supporting documents, and the leave duration is determined in conjunction with health services professionals, the Registrar’s Office, and the student. Administrative leaves of absence may also be granted for outstanding student account balances, university-sponsored events, military leave, and excused absences due to emergencies. Instructors are expected to outline attendance expectations clearly and allow students to make up missed assignments if the absence is reasonable. Students are responsible for submitting appropriate documentation and contacting their instructors to arrange make-up work. The university encourages flexibility and accommodation for students facing such exceptional circumstances, though indefinite leaves are not permitted.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 17]
EXCEPTIONAL CIRCUMSTANCES: The University acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Circumstances that may fall into this category are: • Exceptional medical circumstances, e.g., hospitalization or incapacitation through injury, illness, or mental health crisis. • Close bereavement, e.g., partner, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, and grandchild. Housemates or very close friends may also be considered as ‘close’, though evidence of the relationship may be required. • Victim of a serious crime • Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student • Exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties e.g., major transport incidents, cancelled flights. This does not include everyday issues, e.g., traffic congestion, missed buses or trains. • Legal proceedings requiring

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 15]
with the student’s recovery or safety. If a student determines that medical leave would be beneficial, the student must submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form and the Fulbright Impact Assessment form, along with all medical supporting documents, before the last day of class. Voluntary medical leaves are based on the recommendation of a health services professional that verifies the impact on the capability of completing the academic activities, including but not limited to: • Able to attend the class (Yes/No) • Able to do sustained reading, note-taking, and writing (Yes/No) • Able to perform a task requiring intense concentration for 1-2 hours (Yes/No) Leave duration is determined in conjunction with the health services professional, the Registrar’s Office, and the student. Indefinite leaves are not permitted. 9.3 Administrative Leave of Absence A student may be placed on an administrative leave of absence if he/she has an outstanding student account balance in an enrolled term without informing

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 13]
interviews, funerals, weddings, jury duty, etc. • Military leave, while rare, the student is on-call duty may have the military trainings or orders that conflict with the first weeks of class. Students are aware of the training date in advance. Therefore, they must inform their instructors as much notice as possible. The university and instructor(s) are encouraged to accommodate the students. • Excused absence due to the university-sponsored events/activities for academic, non-academic, and recognized student organizations (including but not limited to student athletes, student council presidents, student club members representing university, etc.). ### Question 82: Are students allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments? If so, under what conditions?  
### Answer: 

Students are allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for their assignments, but under strict conditions to ensure academic integrity and ethical use. The use of generative AI tools must be fully documented, including the reasons for their utilization, the specific elements of the project they contribute to, the tools and platforms employed, the methodology for incorporating AI (such as which aspects of the project are generated, improved, or altered), and how ethical and copyright concerns are addressed.

The documentation requirement is a critical part of the process, ensuring transparency and highlighting the originality and human contributions to the project. This documentation must be comprehensive, covering every aspect of AI usage, and is subject to the regulations described in Fulbright University Vietnam’s Code of Academic Integrity, including updates on the use of generative AI.

Moreover, students must obtain Institutional Review Board (IRB) approval for their research projects, especially when AI tools are used, to ensure ethical considerations and data protection are adequately addressed. This approval process must be initiated early in the Capstone project, ideally during Capstone I, to avoid delays and ensure compliance with academic and ethical standards.

In summary, while AI tools like ChatGPT can be used for assignments, they must be employed responsibly, with full documentation and adherence to the university's academic integrity policies and IRB approval processes. This approach ensures that the use of AI tools does not compromise the educational value and integrity of the assignments.

### Question 83: Where can I get support for mental health treatment?  
### Answer: 

For applied projects, students may request to work with an additional non-academic advisor, such as a mental health practitioner, in consultation with, and subject to the approval of, their primary and secondary academic advisors from the Psychology program. These non-academic advisors can provide support and guidance for mental health treatment-related projects. Additionally, the university may offer resources such as:

- Mental Health First Aid Training Program
- Community Survey on Mental Health Needs
- Public Art Project on Mental Health Themes
- Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services
- Therapeutic Gardening or Nature Program

These resources can help students gather information, develop their projects, and potentially connect them with local mental health services. It's important to note that the primary and secondary academic advisors also play a crucial role in the approval and guidance of these projects, ensuring they are relevant to psychological principles and contribute to the field of applied mental health.

The Evaluation Report, which is a required component of the Capstone by Applied Project, should also include insights or recommendations for future application or research related to mental health treatment. This report should demonstrate the project’s relevance to psychological principles, its potential or observed impact, evidence of rigorous evaluation, and documentation of the student’s involvement and implementation of the program.

In summary, students can get support for mental health treatment through collaboration with a non-academic advisor (such as a mental health practitioner), utilizing university resources like Mental Health First Aid Training or a Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services, and through the guidance and approval of their academic advisors. The Evaluation Report will also serve as a tool to document and reflect on the project's impact and potential for future applications in mental health treatment.

### Question 85: Where can I find resources to facilitate my graduate program after Fulbright undergraduate?  
### Answer: 

The Experiential Learning Program (ELP) at Fulbright can be a valuable resource for facilitating your graduate program after completing your undergraduate studies there. The ELP is designed to provide students with practical, hands-on learning experiences that complement their academic studies. It operates within Fulbright's undergraduate program's standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. For more detailed information about the ELP, you can refer to the official Fulbright website, specifically to the page linked here: https://onestop.fulbright.edu.vn/s/article/Experiential-Learning-Program

This program can offer administrative and academic support, helping students to transition into graduate studies by providing them with valuable skills and experiences that are highly regarded by graduate schools. Additionally, electives offered by Fulbright can help you build a broad and diverse academic background, which can be beneficial when applying to graduate programs.

Regarding the capstone, while it is an integral part of the undergraduate program and not directly related to graduate studies, it does demonstrate your ability to conduct independent research and apply your knowledge, which can be advantageous when applying to graduate schools.

Remember to also maintain regular communication with your advisors and stay organized with your work, as these skills are crucial for success in graduate studies as well.

In summary, the ELP, along with the elective courses and the capstone experience, can provide you with the resources and experiences necessary to facilitate a smooth transition into a graduate program after your undergraduate studies at Fulbright. For specific details and support, refer to the ELP page on the Fulbright website and consult with your academic advisors.

If a teaching assistantship is part of the program, it would likely involve:

- Students being selected or matched to a teaching role based on their academic performance and interest in teaching.
- The major capstone coordinator playing a role in assigning teaching responsibilities to ensure a fair distribution of faculty workload.
- Students being consulted to determine an appropriate solution if their preferred teaching role cannot be immediately accommodated.

### Question 88: How can I get the information of campus usage for events so that I can have proper place to study without getting interrupted?  
### Answer: 

To get the information of campus usage for events so that you can have a proper place to study without getting interrupted, you should follow these steps:

1. **Contact the Event Planning Office**: Reach out to the office responsible for scheduling events on campus. They typically maintain a calendar of events and can provide you with information about upcoming events and their locations.

2. **Check the University Website**: Most universities have a calendar of events on their website. Regularly checking this calendar can help you stay informed about events and plan your study schedule accordingly.

3. **Use the University's Event Scheduling System**: If your university has an online system for scheduling events, you can use it to look up events and see which spaces are booked.

4. **Consult with Academic Advisors**: Your academic advisor may also have information about campus events and can offer advice on the best times and places to study.

5. **Use Campus Maps and Resources**: Many universities provide campus maps that indicate the locations of study spaces and event venues. These maps can help you choose quieter areas for studying.

6. **Sign Up for Event Notifications**: Some universities offer email notifications for upcoming events. Signing up for these notifications can help you stay informed and plan your study schedule accordingly.

7. **Talk to Campus Staff**: Don't hesitate to ask campus staff, such as librarians or administrative assistants, for advice on studying during busy event periods.

By following these steps, you should be able to gather the necessary information to choose study locations that are less likely to be affected by campus events, thereby minimizing interruptions to your study schedule.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 13]

The university and instructor(s) are encouraged to accommodate the students. • Excused absence due to the university-sponsored events/activities for academic, non-academic, and recognized student organizations (including but not limited to student athletes, student council presidents, student club members representing university, etc.). ATTENDANCE: Fulbright students are expected to fully engage with the courses in which they are enrolled at Fulbright, including classes, seminars, talks, and other keystone events. Students are generally expected to miss no more than ten percent (10%) of class, but specific attendance policies may vary depending on the course instructors. 8.1 Types of Absences • General absences must be discussed directly with the instructor(s). This type of absence includes but is not limited to medical appointments, internship interviews, funerals, weddings, jury duty, etc. • Military leave, while rare, the student is on-call duty may have the military trainings or orders that conflict with the first weeks of class. Students are aware of the training date in advance. Therefore, they must inform their instructors as much notice as possible. The university and instructor(s) are encouraged to accommodate the students. • Excused absence due to the university-sponsored events/activities for academic, non-academic, and recognized  

</details> 

### Question 89: I used to take an undergraduate program at another university and I want to transfer credit of studied courses at that university. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified. Credit Transfer from A-level, Advanced Placement (AP), International Baccalaureate (IB), and Cambridge International Exam (CIE) courses will be determined according to the AP/IB/CIE Credit Policy (in development). For more information, please refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal.

### Question 91: I'm a student athlete then how can I bypass all of physical education courses required to graduate?  
### Answer: 

As a student athlete, you may have some flexibility in fulfilling physical education requirements due to your participation in sports. Here are some steps you could take:

1. **Consult with your Athletic Department:** Start by discussing your situation with your athletic department. They may have specific policies or arrangements for student athletes to meet physical education requirements through their athletic participation.

2. **Check with your Academic Advisor:** Your academic advisor can provide guidance on how your athletic participation might satisfy physical education requirements. They may know of alternative courses or ways to earn credits that don't involve traditional PE classes.

3. **Review University Policies:** Look into the university's policies regarding physical education requirements for student athletes. Some institutions may have specific exemptions or alternative options for athletes.

4. **Petition for Exemption:** If there are no clear pathways for exemption, you might consider submitting a petition to the Registrar's Office or the department overseeing physical education courses. Provide documentation of your athletic participation and explain how it meets the intent of the physical education requirement.

5. **Explore Double Counting:** If your athletic participation involves courses or activities that could also count toward your major or minor, you might be able to double count these credits to meet both requirements simultaneously.

6. **Consider Elective Options:** If none of the above options work, you could take elective courses that interest you and that might also contribute to your overall well-being and fitness, thus indirectly meeting the spirit of the physical education requirement.

7. **Stay Informed:** Keep yourself updated on any changes to university policies regarding physical education requirements for student athletes. Policies can change, and new options may become available.

Remember, while you may have some flexibility due to your athletic participation, it's important to adhere to the university's academic standards and requirements. Always seek advice from appropriate university officials to ensure you're making the right choices for your academic and athletic career.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
• Physical Education • Political courses These courses do not count toward the 128-credit requirement. All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 92: I'm currently a third year student and moved out of university dormitory after first year but now I'm struggling to find a new accommodation so can I register again for dormitory and will I still have the financial support?  
### Answer: 

If you're currently struggling to find a new accommodation, you might consider reaching out to the Residential Life staff at your university. They may be able to provide you with information on available housing options or even temporary accommodations while you search for a more permanent solution. Regarding re-registering for the dormitory, most universities have a process for students to return to on-campus housing, especially if they are facing exceptional circumstances such as difficulty finding off-campus housing.

As for financial support, it depends on the university's policies and your individual circumstances. Some universities may offer financial assistance or support for students who are experiencing housing difficulties, especially if they can demonstrate that they are actively seeking accommodation and are unable to secure off-campus housing due to reasons beyond their control.

To find out if you qualify for re-admission to the dormitory and any associated financial support, you should contact the Office of Residential Life and the Financial Aid Office at your university. They can provide you with the most accurate and up-to-date information regarding your situation.

Keep in mind that the university's EXCEPTIONAL CIRCUMSTANCES policy might be relevant here, as you are facing a housing issue that is beyond your control. You may need to provide documentation or evidence of your housing search and the difficulties you are encountering.

Regarding re-admission to full-time status and financial aid, as stated in the provided text, you would need to reapply for admission and financial aid if you withdraw formally or without permission. However, if you are returning due to exceptional circumstances such as housing difficulties, you may be able to make a case for continued support.

In summary, while there is no guarantee of re-admission or continued financial support without going through the proper application and review processes, it is worth reaching out to the relevant university offices to discuss your situation. They may be able to offer solutions or accommodations based on your individual circumstances.

### Question 93: Can you give me the procedure to request for funds to support club activities?  
### Answer: 

The procedure to request funds to support club activities is typically as follows:

1. **Review the Guidelines**: Start by reviewing the project guidelines provided by the university or organization that provides funding. These guidelines will outline the criteria, eligibility, and the application process.

2. **Prepare a Proposal**: Develop a detailed proposal outlining the purpose of the club activity, the budget required, how the funds will be used, expected outcomes, and any other relevant information. The proposal should be clear, concise, and well-organized.

3. **Gather Necessary Documentation**: Compile all necessary documentation, such as the club's constitution, bylaws, a budget breakdown, a timeline for the activity, and any other supporting materials that demonstrate the club's need for funding and the viability of the proposed activity.

4. **Submit the Application**: Submit the completed application and all supporting documents through the appropriate channels. This may involve submitting the application online, via email, or in person to the designated office or person responsible for club funding.

5. **Follow Up**: After submission, follow up with the funding body to ensure that your application has been received and is being processed. Be prepared to provide additional information if requested.

6. **Review and Decision**: The funding body will review the applications and make a decision. This process may take some time, so be patient.

7. **Notification**: Once a decision has been made, you will be notified of the outcome. If the request is approved, you will receive information on how to proceed with the disbursement of funds.

8. **Reporting and Accountability**: After the club activity has taken place, you may be required to submit a report detailing how the funds were used and the outcomes of the activity. This is to ensure accountability and transparency.

9. **Additional Resources**: Some organizations may have additional resources available, such as workshops on grant writing or budgeting, to help clubs prepare stronger applications.

It is important to note that the specific procedures may vary depending on the institution or organization providing the funds, so it is crucial to consult the relevant guidelines and resources provided by your specific context. The referenced documents in the contexts provided do not directly relate to the procedure for requesting funds to support club activities, as they pertain to academic-related forms and processes such as course load requests, credit transfers, and leave of absence applications. These documents are not typically used for financial requests related to club activities.

### Question 94: How many ways are there provided by the university can I get the support in my academic path?  
### Answer: 

There are several ways provided by the university to support students in their academic path. These include:

1. Exceptional Circumstances: The university acknowledges that students may experience circumstances that impact their ability to fulfill academic expectations. This includes exceptional medical circumstances, close bereavement, being a victim of a serious crime, disabilities where reasonable adjustments are not yet in place, and exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties.

2. Capstone Project Support: For the capstone project, students are encouraged to discuss their ideas with IS faculty prior to submitting the proposal to ensure originality and feasibility. Students can also find a secondary advisor at another institution if necessary.

3. Allocation of Advisor Process: Students are asked to provide a first choice of primary and secondary advisor during the application process for the capstone project. The university faculty team will consider expertise, workload distribution, and student choices when allocating advisors.

4. Extensions and Adjustments: The university may consider extensions or adjustments for students facing exceptional circumstances, as outlined in the Exceptional Circumstances section.

5. Communication and Timeliness: Students are expected to communicate with clarity and timeliness with their faculty advisors and to adhere to the academic calendar without requesting unnecessary extensions.

6. Academic Integrity and Plagiarism: The university expects students to submit work that is original, properly cited, and free from plagiarism.

7. Assessment Criteria: The university has specific assessment criteria for the capstone project, including the format, language, rigor of research, and communication skills, which students must meet to be accepted.

These are the primary ways in which the university supports students in their academic journey, particularly through the capstone project process. Each of these points provides a mechanism for students to seek help, guidance, and support in navigating their academic path effectively.

### Question 97: I'm having some bad experience with a professor teaching a course. The problem was his way of delivering does not meet academic standard and I want to say something about this with people having higher authorities. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

If you're experiencing issues with a professor's teaching methods that do not meet academic standards, it's important to address the situation in a constructive and appropriate manner. Here are steps you can take:

1. **Document the Issues**: Keep a detailed record of the incidents that have occurred. Note specific examples of the professor's behavior, such as the issues with eye contact, speaking clearly, inappropriate dress, and incorrect grammar. Also, document any instances where the professor's delivery affected your learning experience.

2. **Seek Support from the University**: Most universities have mechanisms in place to address academic concerns. Here's how you can proceed:

   - **Meet with the Professor**: Schedule a meeting with the professor to discuss your concerns privately. Be specific, polite, and professional. It's possible the professor may not be aware of the impact of their teaching style.

   - **Contact the Department Chair**: If the issue is not resolved with the professor, the next step is to contact the department chair. Explain your concerns and provide the documented evidence you've collected. The chair may be able to mediate the situation or take further action.

   - **Registrar's Office and Dean's Office**: As per the academic integrity policy you've mentioned, you can also involve the Registrar's Office and the Dean's Office. They can organize a panel review if necessary, and the Dean's Office can make a final ruling on matters concerning course policy.

   - **Academic Advising**: Reach out to academic advising. They can offer guidance on how to proceed and may be able to intervene on your behalf.

3. **Follow the University's Procedures**: Familiarize yourself with the university's academic policies and procedures regarding student complaints. Follow these steps carefully, as they are designed to ensure a fair and thorough investigation.

4. **Consider a Formal Complaint**: If the issue persists and the university's mechanisms do not resolve the problem, you may need to file a formal complaint. This usually involves submitting a detailed written complaint to the appropriate office, such as the Office of the Provost or the Dean of Students.

5. **Seek External Support if Necessary**: If the university does not resolve the issue to your satisfaction, you may consider seeking external support, such as contacting a student advocacy group or legal counsel, though this should be a last resort.

6. **Maintain Professionalism**: Throughout the process, maintain professionalism and avoid personal attacks. Focus on the facts and the impact on your academic experience.

Remember, the goal is to improve the educational experience for yourself and potentially for other students. By following the proper channels and documenting your concerns, you can work towards a resolution that respects both your academic rights and the professor's rights to teach.

### Question 98: I'm a third year student and don't know if I should do a capstone project then where should I go to get advice?  
### Answer: 

Students are strongly encouraged to discuss with IS faculty prior to submitting the capstone proposal. As part of the application process, applicants will provide a first choice of primary and secondary advisor. It is not mandatory to have a secondary advisor. After the applications are reviewed, the major capstone coordinator will attempt to accommodate the student’s first and second choice of advisors. If the student’s first or second preference cannot be accommodated due to the necessity of maintaining a fair distribution of faculty workload, the major capstone coordinator will consult with the student to determine an appropriate solution. The primary advisor is your first point of contact, and should hold expertise relevant to your project, for example, in terms of being a specialist in the project’s disciplinary field. The primary advisor will be the primary reviewer of your work in progress, and as such, will be the person with whom you meet most frequently. Expertise does not need to be regional or topical – an advisor may have a strong grounding in the theory or methodological approaches of the capstone rather than a specific research background in that topic. The secondary advisor can offer you additional feedback where necessary and may represent a disciplinary field outside of Social Studies (if your project is interdisciplinary). In cases when there is no available faculty with suitable expertise, students could find a secondary advisor at other institutions.
