### Question 99: I'm a member of Fulbright Basketball Club and going to attend a tournament. I need the official transcript and asking for some absence in classes then where should I get help?  
### Answer: 

For your official transcript, you should contact the Office of the Registrar or the Academic Affairs team at Fulbright University Vietnam. They can assist you with obtaining an official transcript as per your academic records.

Regarding your absence due to attending the basketball tournament, you should follow these steps:

1. **Complete the Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form**: This form is designed for students who need to request an excused absence due to participation in a sponsored academic event or other exceptional circumstances. You will need to provide a summary of the tournament, proof of your attendance (such as an invitation letter or acceptance email), and proof of your travel (like an itinerary).

2. **Submit the Form**: Submit the completed form to the Academic Affairs team at ug.academic.affairs@fulbright.edu.vn well in advance of your absence.

3. **Follow Up**: After your trip, write a reflection paper (300-500 words) about your experience and submit it to the same email address (ug.academic.affairs@fulbright.edu.vn) no later than 7 days after you return.

4. **Inform Your Instructors**: While the form is submitted to the Academic Affairs team, it is also important to inform your course instructors about your planned absence as soon as possible.

5. **Make Up Any Missed Work**: Ensure you make up any missed assignments or exams according to the instructions provided by your instructors.

Remember, the university is committed to supporting student learning, so it's important to follow the proper procedures to ensure your absence is properly documented and accounted for.

Regarding the withdrawal from classes or leave of absence, if you anticipate being away for an extended period, you should also consider filling out the Undergraduate Leave of Absence (LOA) form, which can be found in the provided list of documents. This form should be submitted to the Office of the Registrar if you plan to take a leave from your studies.

Lastly, if you have any questions or need further assistance, don't hesitate to reach out to the Academic Affairs team or the Office of the Registrar directly. They are there to help you navigate your academic journey at Fulbright University Vietnam.

### Question 101: How can I borrow books from the library?  
### Answer: 

To borrow books from the library at Fulbright, you typically need to follow these steps:

1. **Register and Obtain a Library Card**: Ensure you have a valid student ID or library card issued by the Fulbright library. This card is essential for borrowing books.

2. **Locate the Books**: Use the library's online catalog or physical shelves to find the books you need. The catalog will provide information about the availability of the books.

3. **Check Out the Books**: Present your library card at the circulation desk to check out the books. The librarian may ask for your ID to verify your status.

4. **Understand Loan Periods and Limits**: Each book may have a different loan period (e.g., 2 weeks, 1 month). There may also be limits on the number of books you can borrow at one time.

5. **Renew Books**: If you need more time to read the books, you can usually renew them online, through the library's website, or by visiting the circulation desk before the due date.

6. **Return Books**: Return the books on or before the due date to avoid late fees. You can return books to the library's drop box if it's outside of regular hours.

7. **Use Library Resources Responsibly**: Adhere to the library's rules and policies, which may include not damaging books, not removing library property, and respecting quiet hours.

8. **Access Digital Resources**: In addition to physical books, the library may offer access to digital resources, databases, and e-books which can be accessed remotely with your library card.

Remember to check the specific policies and procedures of the Fulbright library, as they may have additional rules or requirements for borrowing books.

### Question 102: How to work with major report?  
### Answer: 

To work effectively with a major report, particularly for a capstone project in film or media production, follow these structured steps:

1. **Understand the Requirements**: Carefully read and understand all the guidelines provided by your institution, including the word count, format, and evaluation criteria.

2. **Plan and Organize**: Break down the report into sections (e.g., Executive Summary, Introduction, Literature Review, Methodology, Findings, Discussion, and Appendices) and allocate time for each section.

3. **Research and Gather Information**: Conduct thorough research on your topic, gather data, and compile all necessary information for each section of the report.

4. **Draft the Executive Summary**: Write a concise summary that clearly outlines the problem, purpose, actions taken, evaluation findings, and their implications. Keep it within the 200-250 words limit.

5. **Develop the Report**: Write each section of the report, ensuring clarity, coherence, and adherence to academic standards. Use the thesis style guidelines for formatting.

6. **Review and Revise**: Regularly review your work for clarity, grammar, and formatting errors. Seek feedback from peers, advisors, and mentors.

7. **Incorporate Feedback**: Use feedback to refine and improve your report. Make necessary revisions, especially to the method chapter and findings.

8. **Prepare Appendices and Documentation**: Include all necessary appendices, legal forms, call sheets, test audience feedback, marketing and distribution plans, and other production documents.

9. **Check Formatting and References**: Ensure that each chapter starts on a new page, chapter numbering and Table of Contents are correct, and references are properly aligned.

10. **Compile and Submit**: Convert your Word document into a PDF and submit it according to the guidelines provided.

11. **Public Defense Preparation**: Prepare for the public defense by practicing your presentation, addressing any questions or concerns, and refining your responses.

12. **Seek Continuous Feedback**: Throughout the process, seek continuous feedback from your advisor(s), secondary advisor, and capstone panel to ensure your work meets the required standards.

13. **Adhere to Deadlines**: Stick to the timeline provided by your institution, including submission deadlines and meeting schedules with advisors.

14. **Maintain Open Communication**: Keep open lines of communication with your advisors and the capstone coordinator to address any issues or concerns that may arise.

By following these steps, you can effectively work with your major report, ensuring a high-quality capstone project that meets the academic and professional standards expected by your institution.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Art & Media Studies Capstone Handbook _v3_210125.pdf, Page: 14]
and distribution) and write about them. The Report should be a production book with writing about what students have researched, observed, experienced, solved, and lessons learned. The report should include all of the pre-production deliverables (mentioned above) plus production documents: - All legal release forms, contracts, or permits necessary for film production - Call Sheets for production - Test audience (if applicable) - Marketing and distribution plans (applied to student producers), etc. The word count (not including production documents) should be under 5000 words. The format can follow the thesis style guidelines (Handbook section 2.2). 4.5. ### Question 103: How many way can I fill in the requirements of EL?  
### Answer: 

The Exploratory requirements for Class of 2024 students consist of completing 16 credits (4 courses) from four different categories: E1-Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, E3- Sciences and Engineering, and E4-Mathematics and Computing, with at most 4 out of 16 credits counted as Pass/No Pass. This means that each student must take one course from each category, totaling four courses, and up to one course can be taken as Pass/No Pass. The number of ways to choose one course from each of the four categories is the product of the number of choices in each category. Assuming each category has a sufficient number of courses to choose from, the number of ways to fulfill the Exploratory requirements for Class of 2024 students is:

Number of ways = (number of courses in E1) * (number of courses in E2) * (number of courses in E3) * (number of courses in E4)

Given that the exact number of courses in each category is not specified, we can only provide a general formula. However, for a specific calculation, you would need to know the number of available courses in each category.

For Class of 2025, 2026, and 2027 students, the requirements are more extensive, requiring 32 credits (8 courses) distributed equally across the four categories (E1, E2, E3, E4), with no more than 8 credits taken as Pass/No Pass. This means each student must take one course from each category, totaling eight courses, and up to 2 courses can be taken as Pass/No Pass.

Number of ways = (number of courses in E1) * (number of courses in E2) * (number of courses in E3) * (number of courses in E4), taken 8 times (one for each category).

Again, without specific numbers for the courses in each category, we can only provide a general formula.

For both cases, the number of ways to fulfill the Exploratory requirements depends on the number of course options available in each category. If each category has 'n' courses available, then:

For Class of 2024: Number of ways = n1 * n2 * n3 * n4

For Class of 2025, 2026, and 2027: Number of ways = (n1 * n2 * n3 * n4) ^ 8

Keep in mind that the actual number of ways to fulfill the requirements will be significantly larger if each category has a substantial number of courses available.

The references provided do not specify the number of courses available in each category, so the exact numerical answer cannot be determined from the given information. The answer is contingent on the availability of courses in each category, which would typically be provided in a course catalogue or by the academic advising office at Fulbright University Vietnam.

For instance, if major A requires certain courses from major B for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major, and these courses are not cross-listed between A and B, they do not count toward the 8-credit limit. 1 In interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors. These courses are usually not cross-listed with the minors and are referred to as 'tagged' by these minors. 13.4  Experiential Learning Requirements Experiential Learning can count toward elective or major requirements (upon advisor approval). Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation
